                                                      <mi>SE</mi>

                                                      <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                                                   </mrow>

                                 <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{eqnarray}{{\Delta}}{E}_{\mathrm{D}}{\mathrm{(SE,\ cathode,\,}}x) &amp;&amp;= {E}_{{\mathrm{eq}}}\left( {{C}_{{\mathrm{interface}}}{\mathrm{(}}{C}_{{\mathrm{SE}}}{\mathrm{,\ }}{C}_{{\mathrm{cathode}}}{\mathrm{,\ }}x{\mathrm{)}}} \right) \nonumber\\ &amp;&amp;\quad\;- {E}_{{\mathrm{interface}}}\left( {{\mathrm{SE}},{\mathrm{\ cathode}},\ x} \right)\end{eqnarray}$$</annotation>
                              </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(4)</span></div>where <i>C</i><sub>SE</sub> and <i>C</i><sub>cathode</sub> are the compositions of SE and cathode materials, normalized to one atom per formula. The <i>x</i> is the molar fraction of the SE. The energies of materials were obtained from Material Project database. More details can be found in previous studies.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202308012-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202308012-bib-0036_R_d119643544e2097" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Adv. Sci. J. Mater. Chem. A">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></div>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202308012-sec-0140">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202308012-sec-0140-title"> Thermodynamic Calculations of Electrochemical Window</h4>
                  
                  <p>The electrochemical window was evaluated using the method in our previous studies.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202308012-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202308012-bib-0036_R_d119643544e2110" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Adv. Sci. J. Mater. Chem. A">36</a>, <a href="#adma202308012-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202308012-bib-0037_R_d119643544e2110" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Engl.">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> A grand potential phase diagram was used to identify the phase equilibria of a given phase in equilibrium with the Na reservoir at chemical potential <i>µ</i><sub>Na</sub> referenced to N<sub>a</sub> metal. The stable electrochemical window of the phase was estimated as the range of <i>µ</i><sub>Na</sub>, where the phase is neither oxidized nor reduced.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202308012-sec-0150">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202308012-sec-0150-title"> Synthesis Methods</h4>
                  
                  <p>All preparation processes and sample treatments were carried out in an Ar-filled glovebox (O<sub>2</sub> &lt; 1 ppm, H<sub>2</sub>O &lt; 1 ppm). The UCl<sub>3</sub>-type halides HCF-Sm/HCF-La and ternary halides NaTaCl<sub>6</sub>, Na<sub>2</sub>ZrCl<sub>6</sub>, and Na<sub>2</sub>HfCl<sub>6</sub> were synthesized by ball-milling the starting materials of NaCl (Sigma Aldrich, 99.9% purity), SmCl<sub>3</sub> (Sigma Aldrich, 99.9% purity) and LaCl<sub>3</sub> (Sigma Aldrich, 99.8% purity), TaCl<sub>5</sub> (Sigma Aldrich, 99.99% purity), ZrCl<sub>4</sub> (Sigma Aldrich, 99.9% purity), and HfCl<sub>4</sub> (Sigma Aldrich, 99.9% purity) at the stated stoichiometric ratio. For ball-milling synthesis, the mixture of precursors was sealed in a zirconia jar (100 mL) under vacuum and ball-milled at 500 rpm for 60 cycles. Each cycle included 10-min milling and 5-min resting. The heterogeneous composite was synthesized by ball-milling as-prepared HCF-Sm/HCF-La and NaTaCl<sub>6</sub>/Na<sub>2</sub>ZrCl<sub>6</sub>/Na<sub>2</sub>HfCl<sub>6</sub> at 500 rpm for another 20 cycles or directly from the precursors at 500 rpm for 90 cycles.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202308012-sec-0160">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202308012-sec-0160-title"> Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>Lab-based XRD measurements were performed on Bruker AXS D8 Advance with Cu Kα radiation (<i>λ</i> = 1.5406 Å). Kapton tape was used to cover the sample holder to prevent air exposure. SEM images and element mappings were obtained by using a Hitachi S-4800 field-emission scanning electron microscope (FE-SEM, acceleration voltage 5 kV) equipped with EDS. The HRTEM images, EDS mapping, and selected area electron diffraction patterns of the studied samples were performed by a Cs-corrected Titan Themis 80–300 TEM, operated at 300 kV, fitted with a Bruker Quantax Super-X EDS detector. The sample powder was directly dispersed on a Cu grid without the assistance of solvent. Elemental maps were acquired at a beam current of 200 pA and an acquisition time of 10–15 min. A standard-based quantification method (Linemarker TEM) was used for the elemental quantification of the acquired elemental maps.</p>
                  
                  <p>The SXRD and PDF were collected using the Brockhouse High Energy Wiggler beamline at the Canadian Light Source (CLS) with a wavelength of 0.3497 Å. The samples were loaded into 0.8 mm inner diameter polyimide capillaries and sealed with epoxy in an Ar-filled glove box. The X-ray diffraction Rietveld refinement and pair distributed function fittings were conducted by GSAS-2 and PDFgui software.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202308012-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202308012-bib-0038_R_d119643544e2187" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - J. Appl. Crystallogr. J. Phys.: Condens. Matter">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> X-ray absorption spectra (XAS) were collected from the Hard X-ray Micro-Analysis (HXMA) and soft X-ray micro characterization (SXRMB) beamlines of CLS, the samples were mixed with BN and pressed into pellets to achieve an absorption length of 1. Samples for Cl K-edge were spread on carbon tape and measured within a vacuum chamber. All XAS data were analyzed with the Athena software, and the EXAFS data were processed using the Artemis program.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202308012-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202308012-bib-0039_R_d119643544e2192" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - J. Synchrotron Radiat.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202308012-sec-0170">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202308012-sec-0170-title"> Electrochemical Characterizations</h4>
                  
                  <p>The temperature-dependent ionic conductivities of prepared SEs were obtained via the EIS measurements of model cells on a multichannel potentiostat 3/Z (German VMP3). The applied frequency range was 1 Hz to 7 MHz and the voltage amplitude was 20 mV. The test cell was fabricated by pressing electrolytes into a pellet (≈400 MPa, 120 mg samples, diameter of 1 cm, thickness ≈0.5–0.6 mm). About 5 mg of acetylene black carbon was then spread onto both sides of the pellet and pressed with ≈150 MPa.</p>
                  
                  <p>The model SSSB was assembled by using the NMNFO as the cathode, Na-Sn (15:4) as the negative electrode, and halide HSEs and/or Na<sub>3</sub>PS<sub>4</sub> as the separator (see diagram of battery architecture in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a>, Supporting Information). A total of 100 mg of the electrolyte powder to be tested was pressed at ≈200 MPa to form an SE layer (1 cm diameter). The cathode composite (NMNFO: SSC: carbon black (CB) = 60:40:2) was uniformly spread onto the surface of one side of the electrolyte layer and pressed with ≈400 MPa for 1 min. Then about 7 mg of the cathode composite was placed on one side of the SSC pellet and pressed at the same pressure, and on the opposite side of SSC, the Na<sub>3</sub>PS<sub>4</sub>, and an excess of Na-Sn alloy (60 mg) were pressed in order. Galvanostatic charge–discharge for SSSB was conducted on the LAND battery test system (CT3002AU-5V10mA) at RT with a stack pressure of ≈80 MPa. The LSV measurement used the same configuration except that the cathode composite was replaced by the mixed powder of the SSC and CB in a weight ratio of 9:1 using a mortar and a pestle. The scan ranges from the open-circuit voltage (OCV) to 6 V (vs. Na/Na<sup>+</sup>, positive scan) or OCV to 0 V (vs. Na/Na<sup>+</sup>, negative scan), respectively. The scan rate was 0.1 mV s<sup>−1</sup>.</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>

         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202308012-sec-0200-title"> Author Contributions</h2>
         
         <p>J.F., S.W., and D.W. contributed equally to this work. J.F. and S.W. conceived the project. J.F. performed the electrolyte synthesis and characterization. S.W. performed the computational simulations. D.W. conducted TEM measurements and analyses under the supervision of M.G. X.L. helped with the fabrication of SSSBs. C.W. and J.L. contributed to the experiment design and data analysis. Y.H., S.Z., F.Z., W.L., and M.L. helped with synchrotron-related characterizations. H.D. and Y.Z. conducted the SEM and XRD measurements. J.F., S.W., D.W., and J.L. formally analyzed all data and wrote the manuscript. M.G., T.K.S., Y.M., and X.S. supervised the project. All the authors participated in the reviewing and editing of the manuscript.</p>
